The Particle 'Thumma' and Its Effect on Sequential Divorce
Examines the particle ثُمّ and its effect on sequential divorce statements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on the particle 'thumma' to determine the legal effect on multiple sequential divorce statements and evaluate the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
'Thumma' indicates delay (tarakhi), which in divorce can sever the connection to a prior condition, preventing subsequent divorces from attaching.

In this passage from Usul al-Shashi, we examine how the simple Arabic particle 'thumma' (then) can fundamentally alter the legal outcome of a series of divorce pronouncements. Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagree on whether 'thumma' breaks the connection between a condition and later statements. Understanding this dispute sharpens your usul al-fiqh tool for analyzing textual particles (al-huruf) and their legal implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the particle and its claimed effect
Recognize that 'thumma' (ثُمّ) is defined as indicating delay (tarakhi) in speech. This linguistic claim is the foundation for the legal rulings that follow.
In Hanafi usul, 'thumma' is distinct from 'fa' (which indicates immediate succession) and 'wa' (which indicates mere conjunction without order).
2
Apply to the basic case: non-consummated wife
If a husband says to his non-consummated wife 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced', only the first divorce falls because she becomes ba'ina (separated) immediately, leaving no subject for further divorces. This is agreed upon.
Non-consummated wife (ghayr madkhul biha) cannot be divorced three times at once; the first divorce makes her irrevocably separated.
3
Apply to consummated wife with condition order variants
For a consummated wife (madkhul biha), the order of condition and divorce matters. Two scenarios are considered: (a) condition presented first, and (b) condition delayed after the series.
Abu Hanifa's ruling differs between these scenarios, while the Sahibayn treat both identically.
4
Compare Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn and identify thamarah al-khilaf
Abu Hanifa holds that delay (tarakhi) severs the connection, so in the condition-first case, the first divorce is attached to the condition and two occur immediately; in the condition-delayed case, two occur immediately and the third is attached. The Sahibayn hold that all are attached to the condition in both cases, so only one divorce falls upon fulfillment.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is how many divorces occur at the moment of utterance versus upon the condition.

(۳) قوله: [في الفصلين] أي: في تقديم الشرط وتأخيره لاتصال الكلام مع كلمة «ثُمّ»، فإن قيل على قول الإمام في صورة تقديم الشرط في المدخول بها وغيرها: إذا تعلقت الأولى بالشرط ينبغي أن لا تقع الثانية والثالثة بل يجب أن يلغو؛ لأنّ كلام الثاني لَمّا انقطع عن الأوّل حتى لا يتعلّق بالشرط لا يشارك الأوّل فيما يتم به، وهي كلمـــة ذلك كالمعاد فيه أيضاً؛ لأنّ ذلك إنما يثبت بشرط الاتصال وهو معدوم فبقي قوله: «ثُمّ طالق» كلام مبتدأ ولو استانف ذلك حقيقةً لا يقع شيء فكذا إذا استانفه حكماً؛ لأنّ الحكمي ملحق بالحقيقي، قلت: على الاتصال وذلك موجود هاهنا فصار المبتدأ كالمعاد في المعطوف فيقع به الثاني ولا يلغـــــو، ولهذا اختص بحرف الفاء الذي يوجب الوصل حتى لو قال: «إن دخلت الدار وأنت طالق» لا يتعلّق بالشرط، وتوضيحه أنه لو قال: «إن دخلت الدار... إلخ» لا يتعلّق الثاني والثالث بالشرط لعدم ما يوجب التعليـــق وهــــو حرف العطف، لكن تثبت له الشركة فيما يتمّ به الأوّل الاتصال صورةً، ويمكن ذلك بدون حــــرف العطـــف مثل: «زيد عالم عاقل فقيه» بأن جعل خبراً بعد خبر فيقعان في الحال كذا في "الفصول" و "المعدن" مختصراً.

And if he said: 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced' in the house. One divorce. May Allah have mercy on him. The divorce because it is separated from what follows. The divorce. If he presents the condition, the first is attached to entry and two occur immediately according to Abu Hanifa; and if he delays the condition, two occur immediately and the third is attached to entry. According to them (the two disciples), all are attached to entry in both cases. (1) His statement: ['And if he said... etc.] This is the second aspect, which is when he delays the condition, i.e., if he said: 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced if you enter the house' — according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, the first occurs and what follows is cancelled because the delay (tarakhi) was in speech, as if he said: 'You are divorced' and was silent upon this measure, so this divorce occurred. Then when she became separated (ba'ina) by the first, no subject remained for what follows because she is not a non-consummated wife (ghayr mawtu'a), so the second and third are cancelled. According to them (the two disciples), one occurs upon entry as we mentioned earlier. (2) His statement: [The first is attached... etc.] i.e., if he says to a consummated wife: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced...' meaning he presents the condition, so the first is attached to the condition, and the second and third occur immediately according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) because they are devoid of attachment (ta'liq) due to their separation from the condition. (3) His statement: [in both cases] i.e., in presenting and delaying the condition due to the connection of speech with the word 'thumma'. If it is said: according to the Imam's statement in the case of presenting the condition for a consummated wife and others: if the first is attached to the condition, the second and third should not occur but rather should be cancelled because the speech of the second, since it is disconnected from the first such that it is not attached to the condition, does not share with the first in what completes it, which is that word [the condition] as if repeated therein; because that is established only on condition of connection, and it is absent. So his statement 'thumma Taliq' remains as an independent speech, and if he were truly to begin anew, nothing would occur. Similarly, if he begins it in a legal sense (hukman) because the legal is annexed to the real. I say: connection exists here, so the beginning becomes like repeated in the conjunct, thus the second occurs and is not cancelled. For this reason, it is specific to the letter fa' which necessitates connection, such that if he said: 'If you enter the house and you are divorced' it is not attached to the condition. Its clarification: if he said: 'If you enter the house... etc.' the second and third are not attached to the condition due to the absence of what necessitates attachment, which is the conjunction letter. But the participation in what completes the first is established by actual connection, and that is possible without the conjunction letter, like: 'Zaid is knowledgeable, rational, jurist' by making it predicate after predicate, so they occur immediately. This is in 'al-Fusul' and 'al-Ma'din' briefly.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage opens by stating that the particle 'thumma' (ثُمّ) indicates delay (tarakhi). The main ruling: if a husband says to his non-consummated wife (ghayr madkhul biha) 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced', only the first divorce falls and the rest are cancelled because she became separated (ba'ina) by the first and no subject (mahall) remains for further divorces. If the woman is consummated (madkhul biha), the ruling differs based on whether a condition (like 'if you enter the house') is attached. Abu Hanifa holds that if the condition is presented first (e.g., 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, then divorced, then divorced'), the first divorce is attached to the condition, and the second and third occur immediately. If the condition is delayed (e.g., 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced if you enter the house'), two divorces occur immediately and the third is attached to the condition. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that in both scenarios, all divorces are attached to the condition (i.e., only one falls upon entry). The hashiah (commentary) explains the reasoning: for Abu Hanifa, the delay (tarakhi) in speech severs the connection, so the subsequent statements become independent and cannot be attached to the same condition. For the disciples, the speech is considered connected despite 'thumma', so all share the condition. The passage also touches on the difference between 'thumma' and 'fa', and provides an example of multiple predicates without conjunction. This is a classic Hanafi usul analysis of textual particles and their effect on legal consequences.

Key Terms
ثُمّ (thumma): Particle indicating delay (tarakhi) between two actions or statements; in this context, it causes the subsequent divorce statements to be temporally separated from the first.
تراخي (tarakhi): Delay in speech; the legal effect that because thumma implies delay, the subsequent statements are independent and not attached to a prior condition.
مدخول بها (madkhul biha): A woman with whom the husband has consummated the marriage; she can be divorced multiple times and her 'iddah allows for remarriage within the same marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a non-consummated wife when the husband says 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced'?
A) Three divorces occur immediately
B) The first divorce occurs, and the second and third are cancelled
C) Only the third divorce occurs conditionally
D) No divorce occurs until the wife enters the house

Key Takeaway
The particle 'thumma' in Hanafi usul indicates a delay that severs the connection of later statements from a prior condition in constructive matters like divorce, leading to different outcomes depending on the order of statements.

The Particle Bal and Retraction in Constructive Speech
Explains the function of 'bal' in retraction and its limitation in constructive speech

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rules that a husband's retraction using 'la bal' after a divorce pronouncement is ineffective for a non-consummated wife, and apply the underlying usul principle to similar cases.

Core Idea
In constructive speech like divorce, retraction is impossible: once uttered, the effect is immediate and irreversible.

Can a husband correct himself after saying 'one divorce' by adding 'no rather two'? The answer depends on whether his speech is informative (ikhbari) or constructive (insha'i). This passage from Usul al-Shashi explains that the particle 'bal' is used for correcting errors in informative contexts, but in constructive acts like divorce, retraction is invalid because the first utterance already created a legal effect. We will explore the reasoning and the different rulings for consummated and non-consummated wives.

Guided Path
1
Identify the utterance and its context
Consider the husband's statement: 'You are divorced once, no rather twice' (to a non-consummated wife). Identify the first part as a divorce pronouncement (insha) and the second as a retraction attempt.
The wife is non-consummated (ghayr madkhul biha), so one divorce makes her ba'ina (irrevocably separated).
2
Classify the speech as constructive (insha)
Recognize that divorce is a form of insha: it creates legal effects immediately upon utterance, unlike informative statements that can be corrected.
The passage explicitly states: 'because the speech is insha and cannot be invalidated after utterance.'
3
Apply the Hanafi rule: insha is irrevocable
Under Hanafi usul, once an insha utterance is complete, it cannot be retracted by subsequent speech. The first divorce stands; the retraction with 'la bal' is ignored.
This contrasts with informative speech where 'bal' corrects the error and the second statement replaces the first.
4
Distinguish between non-consummated and consummated wives
For a non-consummated wife, only one divorce falls because she becomes ba'ina, leaving no subject for further divorces. For a consummated wife, three divorces fall: the first plus the two mentioned in the retraction (since she can take multiple divorces and retraction is invalid, the second part is treated as an addition).
The text says: 'if she was consummated, three occur... by overlapping the first into the two.'
5
Recognize the broader usul principle
This case illustrates the general principle that constructive speech cannot be undone. The ruling is derived via ta'lil (reasoning based on the nature of insha).
The hashiah also contrasts with a debt example where 'la bal' indicates an upgrade (idrab bil-taraqqi) and only the second amount is owed, because debt is not insha but a form of iltizam.

When the word 'la' is joined to it, it becomes a negation in the negation of the first, like: 'Zaid came to me, no rather 'Amr'. Thus say the verifiers. (2) His statement: [by establishing the second... etc.] So when you say: 'Zaid came to me, bal 'Amr' and you intended to inform about Zaid's coming, then it became clear to you that you were mistaken in that information, so you turn away from it to 'Amr, and you say: bal 'Amr. And when you say: 'Zaid did not come to me, bal 'Amr' — its meaning according to the majority is 'bal 'Amr came to me'; according to al-Mubarrad it is 'bal 'Amr did not come to me'. And Abd al-Qahir said: the speech may bear both aspects. Then know that turning away with the word 'bal' from what is before it is valid only in every context where retraction from the first is valid, i.e., where error is possible, like informative speech (ikhbar), not in what does not admit it, like constructive speech (insha). And in cases where the turning away from the first is not indicated, the word 'bal' therein is metaphorically like pure conjunction, so the second is established as added to the first in a cumulative manner without order. Thus in the commentaries of al-Manar. (3) His statement: [And his retraction is not valid... etc.] because the speech is constructive (insha) and cannot be invalidated after utterance without making it in the ruling of being passed over; because it has existed and proceeded from him without justification, and he cannot annihilate it, i.e., keep it in its original non-existence; because existence originates by existence, so he cannot make it as if it were not. As for subsequent non-existence, it does not harm existence; it is realized in its time, and when it is realized, its ruling must follow upon it, which is the occurrence of divorce, due to the impossibility of the ruling lagging behind its cause; because it necessitates it, rather the time of its existence is the same as the time of its existence. Thus in the books of usul. (4) His statement: [Three occur] because retraction is not possible, so the first and the last two occur with it, contrary to if the woman is non-consummated, where one occurs; because retraction from it is not valid, so one occurs and she becomes separated (t bayyana biha) and no subject remains at his saying 'twice', so they do not occur. Thus in al-Fusul.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage discusses the particle 'bal' (بَل) when used for correcting an error (tadaruk al-ghalat). In Arabic, 'bal' with 'la' (لا بل) indicates retraction from a previous statement and substitution of a new one. The ruling: if a husband says to his non-consummated wife (ghayr madkhul biha), 'You are divorced once, no rather twice', only one divorce falls because the first divorce is constructive (insha) and cannot be retracted; once uttered, it is effective and the wife becomes ba'ina, leaving no subject for further divorces. Thus the second part ('twice') is cancelled. If the wife is consummated (madkhul biha), three divorces fall: the first plus the two indicated by 'twice' (since she can take multiple divorces). The hashiah explains that 'bal' primarily functions for turning away (i'rad) from the first statement and is valid only in informative contexts (ikhbari) where retraction is possible, not in constructive contexts (insha'i) like divorce. The passage contrasts this with a debt example: if one says, 'I owe you a thousand, no rather two thousand', only two thousand is owed (the second replaces the first, not adding), due to upgrade (taraqqi). The hashiah also discusses the views of grammarians like al-Mubarrad and Abd al-Qahir on the meaning of 'bal' after negation. The key principle: in constructive speech, once an utterance is made, it cannot be undone; retraction is impossible, so the first statement stands alone.

Key Terms
بل (bal): Particle used for turning away (i'rad) from a previous statement and replacing it with another; when preceded by 'la', it indicates retraction and correction.
إنشاء (insha): Constructive speech that creates a legal effect immediately upon utterance, such as divorce, marriage, oath; it cannot be retracted once complete.
إضراب بالترقي (idrab bil-taraqqi): A type of retraction where the second statement upgrades or increases the first, but without adding them both; the second replaces the first.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a husband says to his consummated wife 'You are divorced once, no rather twice', how many divorces occur?
A) One divorce
B) Two divorces
C) Three divorces
D) No divorce, because he corrected himself

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, constructive speech (insha) like divorce is irrevocable; a retraction using 'la bal' is ineffective, and the first utterance alone determines the ruling, amended only by the capacity of the subject (e.g., consummation).

The Conjunction 'Bal': Correcting Error in Confessions
Definition of 'bal' and its effect in confessions with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the conjunction 'bal', when used in a confession of the same type, replaces the first statement with the corrected amount, and contrast this with Zufar's view that both amounts accumulate.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, 'bal' corrects error by replacing the first statement, not adding to it, in same-type confessions.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi defines the legal function of the Arabic conjunction 'bal' in the context of confessions (iqrar). The key question is whether 'bal' cancels the first statement and substitutes the second, or whether both statements remain binding. The Hanafi school, relying on a Prophetic hadith, holds that the first confession is binding but can be corrected by 'bal' in a way that the corrected amount becomes the sole obligation. Imam Zufar disagreed, arguing that both amounts are owed. This lesson unpacks the definition, evidence, and the practical dispute.

Guided Path
1
Define the particle 'bal'
Read the matn: 'بل لتدارك الغلط'. Note that 'bal' is a conjunction used to correct error (tadarak al-ghalat). Identify that this definition applies to reports (akhbar), not creative utterances (insha').
The particle is a harf atf that indicates correction.
2
Apply to a confession scenario
Consider the case: a confessor says 'I owe one thousand dirhams', then says 'no rather two thousand dirhams'. According to the Hanafi position (matn: 'يجب ألفان'), the corrected amount of two thousand is owed. Zufar holds that three thousand is owed.
Both agree the first confession is binding; the dispute is about how 'bal' operates.
3
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The hadith 'al-mar' yu'khadhu bi iqrarihi' establishes the binding nature of confessions. The first confession cannot be cancelled. However, 'bal' allows correction without cancelling. The Hanafi interpretation: 'bal' establishes the second statement in place of the first, but since the first cannot be cancelled, the practical effect is that the corrected amount alone is binding.
The hadith is cited in the hashiya.
4
Differentiate from Zufar's view
Imam Zufar argues that 'bal' combines both matters, so the total is the sum (3000). The Hanafi response: 'bal' does not combine; it replaces. The first remains only in the sense that it cannot be retracted, but its effect is superseded by the correction.
The example of different types (dirhams and dinars) shows that when types differ, both obligations stand.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Under Hanafi, the confessor owes 2000; under Zufar, 3000. The tarjih is for the Hanafi position due to the binding nature and the linguistic norm of 'bal'.

Even if the divorce is by way of report, two fall due, as we said: correction of error in reports is possible. This is in al-Ma'din.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the conjunction 'bal' (بل) in legal usage, specifically its role in correcting error. The matn states that 'bal' is for correcting error (تدارك الغلط). The commentary explains that when a person confesses to owing a sum and then uses 'bal' to correct it, the second amount is added to the first, not replacing it, because the first confession is binding. The Hanafi position is that the confessor owes the total of both amounts (here, two thousand), while Zufar holds that three thousand are owed because 'bal' aims to correct by combining both meanings—thus the original amount plus the corrected amount. The commentary refutes this by emphasizing that 'bal' establishes the second in place of the first without canceling the first, but the first remains binding due to the prophetic hadith: 'A person is held to his confession.' The analogy is drawn: if someone says 'I owe one thousand dirhams, no rather one thousand dinars,' both sums are due because the two items are of different types, so 'bal' adds, not replaces. The passage then contrasts confession with divorce: if a man says to his non-consummated wife 'You are divorced with one, no rather two,' only one divorce occurs. Because divorce is a creative utterance (إنشاء) that brings an effect into existence; once one divorce exists, the statement cannot be retracted. The error correction ('bal') works only in reports (إخبار), which can be true or false, so it is possible to correct a false report. If the divorce is phrased as a report (e.g., 'I divorced you yesterday with one, no rather two'), then two divorces occur because it becomes an informative statement that can be corrected. This distinction is crucial in Hanafi fiqh: 'bal' operates in the realm of confession (which is a report) but not in the creative act of divorce. The commentary references al-Ma'din for this detail.

Key Terms
بل (bal): A conjunction used for correcting error (تدارك الغلط); in legal usage, it adds the second statement to the first without cancelling the first, in the context of reports.
إقرار (iqrar): A confession or admission, considered a report (khabar) that can be true or false; therefore, it can be corrected using 'bal'.
إنشاء (insha'): A creative utterance that brings an effect into existence (e.g., divorce, sale); it does not admit error correction because once executed, it cannot be undone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 500 dirhams
B) 2500 dirhams
C) 3000 dirhams
D) 3500 dirhams

Key Takeaway
In confessions of the same type, 'bal' corrects error by replacement: the corrected amount is the sole obligation, not the sum of both statements.

The Scope of 'Bal': Reports vs Creative Utterances (Divorce)
Definition of 'bal' and its limitation to reports, with an example from divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish reports (akhbar) from creative utterances (insha') and apply the rule that 'bal' corrects error only in reports, not in creative acts like divorce.

Core Idea
Error correction with 'bal' applies only to reports; creative utterances are irreversible once executed.

The same passage from Usul al-Shashi not only defines 'bal' but also delimits its scope. While 'bal' can correct errors in confessions (which are reports), it cannot correct errors in creative utterances such as divorce. This is because a creative utterance brings about a new legal state (e.g., dissolution of marriage) that cannot be undone by a correction. This lesson explores that critical distinction and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of speech
The texts distinguishes between khabar (report) and insha' (creative utterance). A report can be true or false; a creative utterance creates a new reality. Recognize that confession (iqrar) is a report, while divorce (talaq) is insha'.
In the passage: 'لأنّ هذا إنشاء وذلك إخبار' (because this is insha' and that is khabar).
2
Understand why error correction works in reports
Error (ghalat) occurs in reports because they can be true or false. When someone falsely confesses, correction restores truth. The particle 'bal' enables this correction by allowing the speaker to replace the false statement with the true one.
3
Analyze why divorce is not correctable
Divorce, once pronounced (e.g., 'You are divorced with one'), immediately creates a legal effect. The existence of one divorce cannot be undone by saying 'no rather two'. The second statement is ineffective because the subject (the marriage) has already been affected.
The passage uses the case of a non-consummated wife: after one divorce, there is no waiting period, so the subject ceases to exist.
4
Note the exception: divorce as a report
If the divorce is phrased as a report (e.g., 'I divorced you yesterday with one, no rather two'), then correction is possible because it is an informative statement. This confirms the rule: error correction applies only to reports.
The passage: 'حتى لو كان الطلاق بطريق الإخبار يقع ثنتان' (if it is by way of report, two occur).
5
Derive the usul principle
The principle: 'الغلط إنما يكون في الإخبار دون الإنشاء' (error occurs only in reports, not in creative utterances). This is a key usul principle governing the operation of correction particles like 'bal'.

Section: 'Bal' is for correcting error. 'Bal' is the particle of conjunction to correct error. A proof for our school, not for him. The word 'bal'. That is to correct it. Thousands according to us, and Zufar said: 'Three thousand are obligatory'; because the reality of the word is to correct error by combining both matters. 'Bal' is the particle of conjunction. The one who confesses. That is the confession of one thousand. That is the confession of one thousand. That is the confession of two thousand. By establishing the second in place of the first, and it is not valid to cancel the first, so the second must be validated. That is the confession of one thousand. From two thousand. That is the section on divorce. So it is not valid: by discarding the restriction of bareness. (2) His statement: ['so it is obligatory...'] meaning: both the two thousand along with the first thousand are binding upon him, just as if he said: 'I owe one thousand dirhams, no rather one thousand dinars,' then both sums are binding because of the difference in type. (3) His statement: 'contrary to his statement: You are divorced...' means: if he says to a woman who has not been consummated: 'You are divorced with one, no rather two,' then one falls due; because when he says 'You are divorced with one,' one has occurred, and he cannot turn away from it, and since she is not consummated, there is no waiting period, so the subject matter ceases to exist, and what comes after is void. Because divorce is a creative utterance, and error only occurs in reports, not in creative utterances; because it brings into existence something that was not, and after something exists, it cannot be corrected by making it remain non-existent. As for a report, it can be true or false, so it can be corrected by truth and denial of falsehood. Thus it is possible to correct the word by correcting error in confession, but not in divorce. Even if the divorce is by way of report, two fall due, as we said: correction of error in reports is possible. This is in al-Ma'din.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the conjunction 'bal' (بل) in legal usage, specifically its role in correcting error. The matn states that 'bal' is for correcting error (تدارك الغلط). The commentary explains that when a person confesses to owing a sum and then uses 'bal' to correct it, the second amount is added to the first, not replacing it, because the first confession is binding. The Hanafi position is that the confessor owes the total of both amounts (here, two thousand), while Zufar holds that three thousand are owed because 'bal' aims to correct by combining both meanings—thus the original amount plus the corrected amount. The commentary refutes this by emphasizing that 'bal' establishes the second in place of the first without canceling the first, but the first remains binding due to the prophetic hadith: 'A person is held to his confession.' The analogy is drawn: if someone says 'I owe one thousand dirhams, no rather one thousand dinars,' both sums are due because the two items are of different types, so 'bal' adds, not replaces. The passage then contrasts confession with divorce: if a man says to his non-consummated wife 'You are divorced with one, no rather two,' only one divorce occurs. Because divorce is a creative utterance (إنشاء) that brings an effect into existence; once one divorce exists, the statement cannot be retracted. The error correction ('bal') works only in reports (إخبار), which can be true or false, so it is possible to correct a false report. If the divorce is phrased as a report (e.g., 'I divorced you yesterday with one, no rather two'), then two divorces occur because it becomes an informative statement that can be corrected. This distinction is crucial in Hanafi fiqh: 'bal' operates in the realm of confession (which is a report) but not in the creative act of divorce. The commentary references al-Ma'din for this detail.

Key Terms
إنشاء (insha'): A creative utterance that brings an effect into existence (e.g., divorce, sale); it does not admit error correction because once executed, it cannot be undone.
إخبار (ikhbar): A report or informative statement that can be true or false; it admits error correction via particles like 'bal'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Because the wife must consent to the correction
D) Because the husband must repeat the entire sentence

Key Takeaway
Error correction with 'bal' is limited to reports (akhbar); creative utterances (insha') are irreversible once executed.

The Conjunction 'Lakin' for Istidrak: Definition and Usage Conditions
Definition and conditions of 'lakin' for istidrak

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the function of the conjunction 'lakin' (istidrak) and apply the rules for its usage in nominal and sentential conjunction.

Core Idea
Lakin preempts misunderstanding by affirming the opposite after negation, but only when two differing concepts exist.

This lesson delves into the Hanafi analysis of the conjunction 'lakin' (لكن) as a tool for istidrak — correcting a potential misunderstanding. The passage from Usul al-Shashi defines its function and conditions, distinguishing between nominal and sentential conjunction, and between the lightened and heavy forms. Understanding this will sharpen your ability to parse legal texts where similar conjunctions carry specific semantic weight.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the purpose of istidrak
Istidrak means preempting a false inference. Lakin is used to clarify that a negation applies to one part and affirmation to another, preventing the listener from misunderstanding the scope of the negation.
2
Identify the condition for nominal conjunction
When lakin conjoins two single words (e.g., 'not Zaid but Amr'), it must be preceded by negation. The example given: ما جاءني زيد لكن عمرو.
Nominal conjunction: conjoining individual nouns or adjectives.
3
Identify the condition for sentential conjunction
When conjoining sentences, lakin can appear after both negation and affirmation. The difference (تخالف) can be between positive and negative or between two positive concepts.
Sentential conjunction: conjoining full clauses.
4
Distinguish between the lightened and heavy forms
Lightened (مخففة) is a true conjunction; heavy (مثقلة) is a particle resembling a verb (like إنّ), but both share istidrak. Scholars included heavy among conjunction analogues.
Heavy form: لَكِنَّ (with shaddah on nun).
5
Note that negation is not proven by lakin
The negation of what precedes is established by its own evidence (دليل); lakin only affirms what follows. Lakin does not create the negation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(1) قوله: [للاستدراك ... إلخ هذا اصطلاح الخليل أي: طلب درك السامع بدفع ما عسى أن يتوهم من الكلام السابق فلا بد له من مفهومين متخالفين، فلو عطف بها مفرد على مفرد وجب وقوعها بعد النفي كما أشار إليه في المتن، كما في «ما جاءني زيد لكن عمرو» أي: «جاءني عمرو»، ولو عطف بها جملة على أخرى جاز الأمران فيها وقوعها بعد النفي وبعد الإثبات، والتخالف أعم من أن يكون بالإيجاب والسلب أو ما يجري مجراهما من التخالف بين الثبوتيتين كالزوجية والفردية والإنسانية والفرسية، وهي إن كانت مخففة فهي عاطفة وإن كانت مشدّدة فهي مشبهة مشاركة للعاطفة في الاستدراك، فإن قيل: الكلام هاهنا في بيان حروف العاطفة وكلمة «لكن» إنما تكون عاطفة إذا كانت مخففة، وأما إذا كانت مثقلة فهي من الحروف المشبهة بالفعل، وقد ذكر المصنّف وسائر أيمة الأصول المثقلة في نظائر العطف، قلت: نعم! كلمة «لكن» العاطفة لا تكون إلا مخففة إلا أن المشايخ رحمهم الله تامحوا في ذلك فذكروا المثقلة في نظائر العطف؛ لأنّ كليهما للاستدراك، كذا في "المعدن".
Section: 'Lakin' is for istidrak (reconsideration). That is, the ruling. That is, 'lakin'. That is, 'lakin'. Section: 'Lakin' is for istidrak after negation, so its required consequence is affirming what comes after it. As for negating what is before it, that is established by its own proof. And conjunction with this word is realized only when the speech is coherent. That is, coherence in mutual conjunction. So if the speech is coherent, the negation is linked with the affirmation that follows it; otherwise (if not coherent). (1) His statement: '[for istidrak ... etc.]' This is the terminology of al-Khalil, i.e., seeking the understanding of the listener by repelling what might be imagined from the previous speech. So it must have two differing concepts. If it is used to conjoin a single word to a single word, its occurrence must be after negation, as indicated in the text, like 'Zaid did not come to me, but Amr came' meaning 'Amr came'. If it conjoins a sentence to another, both cases are permissible: its occurrence after negation and after affirmation. The difference is broader than being by affirmation and negation, or what runs in their course, like the difference between two affirmative things such as conjugality and singleness, humanity and horseness. Whether it is lightened (mukhaffafa) it is a conjunction, and if it is heavy (muthaqqala) it is a particle resembling a verb, sharing in istidrak with the conjunction. If it is said: the discourse here is about explaining the letters of conjunction, and the word 'lakin' is only a conjunction when lightened; as for when it is heavy, it is from the particles resembling a verb, and the author and other imams of usul have mentioned the heavy one among the analogues of conjunction. I say: Yes! The conjunctive 'lakin' is only lightened, except that the mashayikh (may Allah have mercy on them) were lenient in that, so they mentioned the heavy one among the analogues of conjunction because both are for istidrak. This is in al-Ma'din.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage defines the conjunction 'lakin' (لكن) and its function of istidrak (استدراك), i.e., correcting a misunderstanding or preempting a false inference. The matn states that 'lakin' is used after negation and its effect is to affirm what follows it; the negation of what precedes is established by its own proof, not by 'lakin'. The commentary expands by referencing al-Khalil's definition: istidrak means 'seeking the understanding of the listener by repelling what might be imagined from the previous speech.' For 'lakin' to function, there must be two mutually exclusive concepts (مفهومين متخالفين). When conjoining single words (i.e., nominal conjunction), 'lakin' must appear after negation; for example, 'ما جاءني زيد لكن عمرو' means 'Zaid did not come to me, but Amr came' – affirming the coming of Amr. When conjoining sentences, it can appear after both negation and affirmation. The difference (التخالف) can be between positive and negative, or between two positive facts like 'married' vs 'single,' 'human' vs 'horse.' The commentary also addresses the distinction between the lightened (مخففة) form of 'lakin' which is a conjunction, and the heavy (مثقلة) form which is a particle resembling a verb (inna and its sisters). The author and other usul scholars have included the heavy form among conjunction analogues due to leniency, as both share the function of istidrak. This passage is crucial for understanding how 'lakin' operates differently from 'bal' (covered earlier): 'bal' corrects error in reports and can occur after affirmative statements, while 'lakin' typically follows negation in single-word conjunctions and serves to prevent a misunderstanding, not to correct an error.

Key Terms
لكن (lakin): A conjunction used for istidrak (دفع توهم) after negation; it affirms what follows it while the negation of what precedes is proven by other evidence.
استدراك (istidrak): The act of correcting a misunderstanding or preempting a false inference by clarifying the intended meaning after potential ambiguity.
اتساق (ittisaq): Coherence and proper linkage of speech parts so that negation and affirmation are logically connected without contradiction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) It must be used after a negation
C) It must be used after an interrogative
D) It can be used in any context

Key Takeaway
Lakin is a conjunction that preempts misunderstanding (istidrak) by affirming the opposite after a negation, but its negation of the prior is independently proven.

The Conjunction 'Lakin' for Istidrak: Definition and Application
Defining and ruling on the conjunction 'lakin' for correction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for 'lakin' as a conjunctive particle for istidrak and apply the coherence condition to evaluate whether a negation applies to the cause or the principal in a legal statement.

Core Idea
'Lakin' affirms what follows after negation; the preceding negation stands on its own proof, not on 'lakin'.

Understanding the conjunction 'lakin' (but) is essential in Hanafi usul for interpreting legal statements where a party corrects a potential misunderstanding. This lesson defines istidrak, distinguishes noun vs. sentence conjunction, and applies the condition of ittisaq (coherence) to classic fiqh examples from Imam Muhammad's al-Jami'.

Guided Path
1
Define 'lakin' for istidrak
Identify that 'lakin' is a conjunctive particle (when light) used for istidrak (correction of a listener's misunderstanding). It affirms what follows after negation, while the negation before is proven by its own evidence.
Istidrak requires two opposing concepts; 'lakin' itself does not negate.
2
Distinguish noun vs. sentence conjunction
When joining nouns, 'lakin' must follow negation. When joining sentences, it may follow either negation or affirmation, provided the speech is coherent.
The condition of ittisaq is crucial: negation and affirmation must relate logically without contradiction.
3
Analyze the coherence condition (ittisaq)
Coherence requires (1) connectedness of the parts and (2) that the place of negation differs from the place of affirmation to avoid contradiction. If lacking, 'lakin' is not valid.
Example from the text: 'جاءني زيد لكن عمروا لم يأت' is incoherent because both are about coming.
4
Apply to fiqh examples from al-Jami'
Examine the three cases: debt, slave-girl price, and slave ownership. In each, the negation (e.g., 'No') targets the cause (loan, price, ownership), not the principal (the money or the slave itself), allowing coherence.
The negation is about the specific reason, so the principal obligation remains affirmed by other evidence.
5
Contrast 'lakin' with 'bal'
'Bal' (but rather) negates the first and affirms the second by its own nature, while 'lakin' only affirms the second; negation of the first is independently proven.
This difference affects how legal statements are parsed.

ألف أو صفة أو بيان له. ١٢ أي ليس لي عليك ألف لأجل القرض. ١٢ أي المقر يكون الألف عليه قرضا. ١٢ أي كلام المقر له. ١٢ ألف قرض» فقال فلان: «لا ولكنّه غصب لزمه المال؛ لأن الكلام متسق (E) فظهر أن النفي كان في السبب دون نفس المال، وكذلك لو قال: «لفلان علي ألف المشار إليها. ١٢ الذي أقر به المقر وهو القرض. ١٢ أي ليس لي عليك ألف من ثمن الجارية. ١٢ من ثمن هذه الجارية» فقال فلان: «لا ، الجارية جاريتك ولكن لي قرض. ۱۲ أي المقر بألف من ثمنها. ١٢ الذي أقربه المقر وهو كونها من ثمن الجارية. ١٢ عليك ألفاً يلزمه المال فظهر أن النفي كان في السبب لا في أصل المال، ولو أي الألف المقر بها . ١٢ ذو اليد. ١٢ أي العبد الذي في يدي. ١٢ أي المقرله. ١٢ كان في يده عبد فقال: «هذا لفلان»، فقال فلان: «ما كان لي قط ولكنه لفلان رجل. ۱۲ أي العبد المذكور. ١٢ أي العبد المذكور. ١٢ (۱) قوله: [لزمه المال] فالنفي في مسئلة "الجامع" وهو ما قال فلان: «لا» والإثبات هو قوله: «لكنه غصب» فهاهنا تعلّق النفي بمحل الإثبات؛ لأنّ محلّ الإثبات هو السبب أي القرض لا أصل المال وهو لزوم ألف درهم فيكون النفي وهو قوله: «لا» متعلقا بالسبب أي بالقرض لا بأصل الإقرار وهو لزوم ألف درهم. ١٢ (۲) قوله: [لأنّ الكلام... إلخ ] أي: كلام المقر وكلام المقرّ له متوافقان لا متنافيان؛ لأنهما يوافقان في أصل المال وإن اختلفا في السبب؛ لأنّ المقرّ له إنما نفى سبباً وهو القرض وأثبت سبباً آخر وهو الغصب ولا يتعرّض كلامه أصل المال، كذا في "المعدن". ١٢ (۳) قوله: [دون نفس المال] فكان الكلام متسقاً والمقصود من الأسباب أحكامها فعند اتحاد ما هو المقصود لا يبالي باختلاف الأسباب على أنّ التوفيق في التصحيح أيضاً ممكن؛ لأن من الجائز أنه أخذ الألف من مال المقرّ له عند غيبته بنية القرض بناء على ما بينهما من الانبساط لا أنّ المقرّ أخذه غصباً بناءً على عدم الإذن والإجازة بالأخذ، كذا في "المعدن". ١٢ (٤) قوله: [وكذلك] أي: مثل المذكور في اتساق الكلام وفي نفي السبب دون أصل المال، كذا في "الحصول". ۱۲ عن (٥) قوله: [ولكنّه ... إلخ] «لكنّه» نفي، لكنّه عن نفسه لقوله: «ما كان لي»، قد يحتمل أن يكون نفياً نفسه مع التحويل إلى المقرّ له الثاني، ويحتمل أن يكون نفياً عن نفسه بدون التحويل، فإذا وصل قوله: «لكنه لفلان كان بيان أن نفي الملك عن نفسه كان مع التحويل إلى الثاني بإثبات الملك، فيكون العبد للمقر له الثاني. ۱۲
Chapter: 'Lakin' for Istidrak. i.e., the ruling. i.e., 'lakin'. i.e., 'lakin'. Chapter: 'Lakin' for Istidrak after negation, so its positive import affirms what comes after it. As for negation of what is before it, it is established by its own evidence. Conjunction with this word is only realized when there is coherence (ittisaq) of speech. If the speech is coherent, the negation relates to the affirmation that follows it; otherwise, if it is not coherent... (Commentary...)
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi explains the particle 'lakin' (but) used for istidrak (correction/exception). The author states that 'lakin' is used after negation to affirm what follows, while the negation of what precedes remains established by its own proof. The conjunction is valid only when the speech is coherent (mutasq), meaning the negation and affirmation are related without contradiction. The hashiya expands: 'lakin' requires two opposing concepts; when joining nouns, it must follow negation, but when joining sentences, it may follow both negation and affirmation. The difference between 'lakin' and 'bal' (but rather) is highlighted: 'bal' negates the first and affirms the second by its very nature, while 'lakin' only affirms the second. Three illustrative fiqh examples from Imam Muhammad's al-Jami' are given: (1) one says 'You owe me 1000 as a loan' and the other says 'No, but it is usurpation' – the negation is about the cause (loan) not the principal, so the money is due. (2) Similar with '1000 from price of a slave-girl'. (3) A person says 'This slave belongs to so-and-so' and another says 'It was never mine, but it is for so-and-so' – the negation of ownership is converted to affirmation for the second. All examples show that negation targets the specific cause, not the underlying debt or ownership.

Key Terms
استدراك (istidrak): A rhetorical device to correct a possible misunderstanding by the listener from the preceding speech, requiring two opposing concepts.
اتساق (ittisaq): Coherence of speech: the parts must be connected and non-contradictory, allowing the conjunction to be meaningful.
عاطفة (atifa): A conjunctive particle that joins two elements, here specifically 'lakin' in its light form.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the fiqh example from al-Jami', the respondent says: 'No, but it is usurpation' regarding a 1000 dirham debt. What does 'No' negate?
A) The existence of the 1000 dirham debt
B) The cause of the debt (loan), not the principal
C) Both the cause and the principal
D) The respondent's own liability

Key Takeaway
When using 'lakin' after negation, the negation targets the cause or specific aspect, not the fundamental claim; coherence ensures the statement is legally meaningful.

The Particle 'Lakin' and the Requirement of Semantic Consistency
Explains the rule of 'lakin' requiring consistency with an example from marriage authorization.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that 'lakin' requires semantic consistency and determine when a statement using 'lakin' is invalid as isti'naf.

Core Idea
'Lakin' demands consistency; affirming what you just negated makes the speech void.

In Hanafi usul, the particle 'lakin' is used for istidrak (correction), but it has a strict condition: the two parts of the statement must be semantically consistent. If someone negates a contract and then affirms the same contract even with a different attribute, the inconsistency renders the affirmation invalid. This lesson explores this rule through the example of a master's authorization of a slave-girl's marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two parts
Separate the statement before and after 'lakin'. The first part is a negation, the second part is an affirmation.
The negation is 'I do not authorize the contract for 100 dirhams.' The affirmation is 'but I authorize it for 150 dirhams.'
2
Check if they refer to the same subject
Determine if the subject (the marriage contract) is the same in both parts. The mahr is different, but the essence is the same marriage.
In Hanafi usul, mahr is considered a surplus attribute (za'id), not part of the essence.
3
Apply the consistency rule
Since the two parts refer to the same subject, the negation and affirmation are contradictory. Therefore, the speech is inconsistent (ghayr muttasiq).
The rule: 'lakin' requires that the second part corrects or excepts a different aspect; it cannot affirm what was just negated.
4
Determine the function of 'lakin'
When inconsistency occurs, 'lakin' cannot function as istidrak. Instead, it becomes isti'naf (starting anew), which means the second part is an independent statement that does not relate back to the first.
In this case, the affirmation is invalid, and the negation stands as a rejection of the contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل لكن للاستدراك بمئة درهم ولكن أجيزه بمئة وخمسين بطل العقد ؛ لأن الكلام غير متسق فإن نفى الإجازة وإثباتها بعينها لا يتحقق فكان قوله: «لكن أجيزه» إثباته بعد نفيه فيرد قوله لا أجيز العقد بمئة درهم رد العقد، وكذلك لو قال: «لا أجيزه ولكن أجيزه إن زدتني خمسين على المئة» يكون فسخا للنكاح لعدم احتمال البيان؛ لأن من شرطه الاتساق ولا اتساق. قوله: [بطل العقد؛ لأنّ الكلام غير متسق] أي: غير متسق أي: غير مرتبط بما قبله أي: من المعنى وإن كان متصلاً صورةً . قوله: [إثباته... إلخ] فيه إشكال وهو أنا لا نسلّم ذلك؛ لأنه ردّ النكاح المقيد بمئة، وأجاز النكاح المقيد بمئة وخمسين فلا يكون نفي الإجازة وإثباتها بعينها في شيء واحد، قلنا: بأن المهر في باب النكاح من الزوائد، ولهذا يصح النكاح بدون ذكره ومع نفيه فكان النفي من أصل النكاح، فكان قوله: «لكن أجيزه... إلخ» إثباته بعينه بعد نفيه فلا يعتبر ؛ لأنّ نكاح الأمة كان موقوفاً على إجازة المولى وقد انفسخ بالردّ والمفسوخ لا تلحقه الإجازة، فيكون «لكن» للاستيناف لا للعطف.
Section: 'Lakin' is for istidrak. [If someone says] 'with one hundred dirhams but I authorize it with one hundred and fifty', the contract is void because the speech is inconsistent. Indeed, the negation of authorization and its affirmation of the same thing do not occur, so his saying 'but I authorize it' is its affirmation after its negation, so his saying 'I do not authorize the contract with one hundred dirhams' is a rejection of the contract. Similarly, if he says: 'I do not authorize it but I authorize it if you increase fifty on the hundred', it is a rescission of the marriage because it does not admit specification; since one of its conditions is consistency, and there is no consistency. He said: [The contract is void because the speech is inconsistent] meaning it is not consistent, i.e., not connected to what precedes it in meaning, even if it is connected in form. He said: [Its affirmation... etc.] There is an objection: we do not concede that; because he rejected the marriage restricted to one hundred and authorized the marriage restricted to one hundred and fifty, so the negation of authorization and its affirmation are not of the same thing. We say: The mahr in the chapter of marriage is among the appendages, and for this reason the marriage is valid without mentioning it, so the negation was from the essence of the marriage. Thus his saying 'but I authorize it... etc.' is its affirmation after its negation, so it is not considered, because the marriage of the slave-girl was suspended on the master's authorization and was annulled by the rejection, and that which is annulled cannot be joined by authorization. So 'lakin' here is for isti'naf (starting anew), not for 'atf (coordination).
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from al-Shashi's matn with commentary. It explains the linguistic rule concerning the particle 'lakin' (but/however) when used for istidrak (correction/exception). The key principle is that 'lakin' requires consistency (ittisaq) between its two parts in meaning. The example given is from the fiqh context of a master authorizing a slave-girl's marriage. If the master says 'I do not authorize the marriage for 100 dirhams but I authorize it for 150 dirhams', the speech is inconsistent because the negation and affirmation refer to the same marriage contract. Although the mahr differs, the mahr is considered a secondary element (za'id), so the negation is from the essence of the marriage. Hence, the contract is void. In the second example, a conditional authorization after rejection is a rescission (faskh) of the marriage because the two parts are inconsistent and cannot be reconciled through specification (bayan). The commentary resolves an objection: the rejection was for a marriage with 100 mahr, the affirmation for 150 mahr, so they are different. The response is that mahr is peripheral, so the subject is the same marriage. Therefore, the ruling is that 'lakin' here functions as isti'naf (beginning anew) not 'atf (coordination), and the contract is void.

Key Terms
لکن (lakin): A particle for istidrak (correction/exception) that requires consistency between its two parts
استدراك (istidrak): Correction or exception; a linguistic function that modifies or corrects a preceding statement

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the contract void when the master says 'I do not authorize it for 100 dirhams but I authorize it for 150 dirhams'?
A) Because the mahr is invalid
B) Because the speech is inconsistent
C) Because the master did not specify which slave-girl
D) Because 'lakin' is not allowed in contracts

Key Takeaway
The particle 'lakin' used after negation requires that the affirmed subject be different in essence; otherwise, the affirmation is invalid and the contract is void.

The Particle 'Aw' in Hanafi Usul: Definition, Dispute, and Applications
Definition and expansion of the particle 'aw' with a madhhab dispute and fiqh applications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the function of 'aw' and distinguish its two modes of tanawul (badal and umum) in fiqh applications.

Core Idea
'Aw' is for one of two without specification; gives choice in constructions, requires clarification in reports; tanawul: badal or umum.

In this lesson, we explore the particle 'aw' (or) as a key term in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The text defines its core function and contrasts it with the view that it indicates doubt. Through concrete examples of manumission and agency, we see how the mode of tanawul (badal vs umum) leads to different legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the function of 'aw'
The text states 'aw' is for taking one of two mentioned things (li'tanawuli ahadil-madhkurayn). Note that it does not specify which one.
2
Distinguish the two contexts
In reports (akhbar), 'aw' may imply doubt due to unknown information; in constructions (insha'), it gives choice (takhyir) or permissibility (ibaha).
3
Analyze the madhhab dispute
The Hanafi position is that 'aw' is not originally for doubt; the opposite view is unsound because doubt is not an intended meaning in speech.
4
Apply the two modes of tanawul
In manumission, tanawul is on badal (alternation) – only one slave is freed, and the master specifies. In agency, tanawul is on umum (generality) – each slave can be sold individually, but the agency ends after one sale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل أو لتناول أحد المذكورين ولهذا لو قال: «هذا حر أو هذا» كان بمنزلة قوله: «أحدهما حر» حتى كان له ولاية البيان، ولو قال: «وكلت ببيع هذا العبد هذا أو هذا» كان الوكيل أحدهما ويباح البيع لكل واحد منهما ولو باع أحدهما ثم عاد العبد إلى ملك الموكل لا يكون للآخر أن يبيع لأنه انتهى التوكيل ببيعه مرة. قوله [لتناول... إلخ ] أي: لنسبة أمر إلى أحد الشيئين لا على التعين أو لنسبة أحد الأمرين إلى شيء، وبالجملة مفاده ومحصول معناه اعتبار المفهوم المردود أخذه من الدوران بين الشيئين فيؤول المعنى إلى مفهوم أحدهما أو معنى أحدهما لا على التعيين، وهذا مفهوم مجمل مبهم غير صالح لنزول الحكم الشخصي عليه كالحرّية والطلاق، ولهذا يحول الأمر إلى بيان القائل وتعيينه ويكون له ولاية ويجيزه القاضي عليه ففي المفردين تفيد ثبوت الحكم لأحدهما، كقولك: «جاءني زيد أو بكر»، كما تقول: زيد قاعد أو قائم»، وفي الجملتين تفيد حصول مضمون أحدهما كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَنِ اقْتُلُواْ أَنفُسَكُمْ أَوِ اخْرُجُوا مِن دِيَارِكُم﴾ [النساء : ٦٦]، هذا هو مذهب عامة أهل اللغة وأئمة الأصول وهو مختار شمس الأئمة وفخر الإسلام وذهبت طائفة من الأصوليين وجماعة من النحويين إلى أنها موضوعة للشكّ وهو ليس بسديد؛ لأنّ الشك ليس معنى يقصد بالكلام وضعاً، بل هي موضوعة لأحد المذكورين من غير تعيين، نعم في الأخبارات يجيء الشكّ باعتبار محلّ الكلام وهو الخبر المجهول، ولذا لزم منه التخيير في الإنشاء؛ لأنّ الإنشاء لإثبات الكلام ابتداءً فلا يحتمل الشك، فإنّ محلّه الخبر فـ«أو» في الإنشاء للتخيير أو الإباحة مثلا على حسب ما يناسب المقام ففي الخبر المجهول لزم البيان وفي الإنشاء لزم التخيير بين أحد الأمرين فافهم. قوله: [كان له ولاية البيان] أي: يبيّن أحدهما أيهما شاء مباركاً كان أو بشيراً، ثمّ تناوله لأحد المذكورين إما على سبيل البدل كما في مسألة الحرّية، وإما على سبيل العموم كما يأتي في مسئلة التوكيل فلا يحتاج إلى بيان المؤكل. قوله: [ويباح البيع ... إلى آخره] دفع لما يقال: إذا كان الوكيل أحدهما فلا يصح البيع لكلّ واحد منهما قبل بيان المؤكل فدفع بقوله: «ويباح البيع... إلخ». قوله : [لكلّ واحد ولا يشترط اجتماعهما أنّ «أو» في موضع الإنشاء للتخيير، والتوكيل إنشاء. قوله: [لا يكون للآخر ... إلخ] عملاً بتناول «أو» لأحد المذكورين على سبيل العموم، فإن قلت: فما الفرق بين مسئلة الحرية ومسئلة التوكيل في كون تناول أو لأحد المذكورين في الأولى على سبيل البدل...
Section: 'Or' is for taking one of the two mentioned things. Hence, if someone says: 'This is free or this', it is like his saying: 'One of them is free' such that he has the authority of clarification. And if he says: 'I appointed you to sell this slave, this or this', the agent is one of them, and the sale is permissible for each one of them. If one of them sells, then the slave returns to the ownership of the principal, it is not permissible for the other to sell because the agency ended with its sale once. He said: [For taking... etc.] i.e., for attributing a thing to one of two things without specification, or for attributing one of two things to a thing. In summary, its purport and the gist of its meaning is considering the concept taken from the fluctuation between two things, so the meaning reduces to the concept of one of them or the meaning of one of them without specification. This is a vague and ambiguous concept not suitable for the application of a specific ruling like freedom or divorce, therefore the matter is referred to the speaker's clarification and specification, and he has authority, and the judge may enforce it upon him. In single words, it indicates the establishment of a ruling for one of them, like your saying: 'Zaid or Bakr came to me', and like your saying: 'Zaid is sitting or standing'. In sentences, it indicates the occurrence of the content of one of them, like the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'Or kill yourselves or leave your homes' (An-Nisa 66). This is the madhhab of the majority of linguists and imams of usul, and it is the choice of Shams al-A'imma and Fakhr al-Islam. A group of usul scholars and a company of grammarians held that it is placed for doubt, but this is not sound because doubt is not a meaning intended in speech by original placement. Rather, it is placed for one of the mentioned things without specification. Yes, in reports, doubt occurs by virtue of the context of speech, which is the unknown information, and from this it necessitates choice in constructions, because construction is for establishing speech originally and does not admit doubt; its place is the report. So 'aw' in construction is for choice or permissibility, for example, according to what suits the context. In the case of the unknown report, clarification is necessary, and in construction, choice between one of two matters is necessary. Understand this. He said: [He has the authority of clarification] i.e., he may clarify whichever he wishes, whether its name is Mubarak or Bashir. Then its taking of one of the mentioned things is either on the way of alternation (badal) as in the case of freedom, or on the way of generality (umum) as will come in the case of agency, so he does not need the principal's clarification. He said: [The sale is permissible... to the end] is a rebuttal of what is said: if the agent is one of them, the sale is not valid for each one before the principal's clarification. So he rebuts with his saying: 'the sale is permissible... etc.' He said: [For each one, and their gathering is not required] because 'aw' in the position of construction is for choice, and agency is construction. He said: [It is not for the other... to the end] acting upon the taking of 'aw' for one of the mentioned things on the way of generality. If you say: What is the difference between the case of freedom and the case of agency in that the taking of 'aw' for one of the mentioned things in the first is on the way of alternation...
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is a definition and exposition of the particle 'aw' (or) in usul al-fiqh. The matn states that 'aw' is for taking one of two mentioned things (li'tanawuli ahadil-madhkurayn). The commentary expands on this by categorizing its usage: in single words (mufradat) it indicates that a ruling applies to one of them, as in 'Zaid or Bakr came', and in sentences (jumal) it indicates the occurrence of the content of one of them, as in the Quranic verse. The Hanafi position (followed by Shams al-A'imma and Fakhr al-Islam) is that 'aw' is not originally for doubt (shakk); rather, doubt arises in reports due to the uncertainty of the speaker. In constructions (insha'), such as commands or permissions, 'aw' gives choice (takhyir) or permissibility (ibaha). The practical fiqh examples are: 1) Manumission: if a master says 'this slave is free or this', it is like saying 'one of them is free' and the master has the right to specify which one. The taking (tanawul) of 'aw' here is on the basis of alternation (badal) – meaning only one of them is intended, but which one is unspecified. 2) Agency: if a principal says 'I appoint you to sell this slave or this', the agent has permission to sell either one; the taking here is on the basis of generality (umum) – meaning each one can be sold by the agent, but only one sale is effective because the agency ends after one sale. The commentary addresses an objection: if the agent is one of them (i.e., only one agent?), the sale should not be valid for each one before the principal clarifies. The response is that 'aw' in construction gives choice, so each sale is permissible individually, but not both. The ruling is clear: the agency ends after the first sale, so the other agent (or the same agent for the other slave) cannot sell again.

Key Terms
أو (aw): A particle for taking one of two mentioned things without specification; in constructions it gives takhyir (choice) or ibaha (permissibility)
تناول (tanawul): The operation of 'aw' in taking one of the mentioned things; can be on the basis of badal (alternation) or umum (generality)
تخيير (takhyir): Choice; the effect of 'aw' in constructions, giving the addressee the option to choose one of the alternatives

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which case does 'aw' take on the meaning of generality (umum) rather than alternation (badal)?
A) Manumission
B) Agency
C) Both
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The particle 'aw' in Hanafi usul is fundamentally for indicating one of two things without specification, and its operation (tanawul) can be on the basis of badal or umum, with distinct fiqh effects.

The Meaning and Legal Application of 'Aw' (أو) in Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh
Defining the particle أو and its usage in akhbar and insha with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the particle 'aw' in legal texts: classify it as indicating one of two without specification in akhbar and choice/permission in insha', and apply the Hanafi position to examples of manumission, agency, divorce, and oaths.

Core Idea
'Aw' in insha' gives choice; in akhbar it indicates one of two without doubt—context determines its legal effect.

Particles like 'aw' may seem trivial, but their precise legal impact is debated. In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi definition of 'aw' as a particle that indicates one of the mentioned things without specification. We will see how this understanding shapes rulings in manumission, agency, divorce, and oaths, and contrast it with the view that 'aw' primarily denotes doubt. By mastering this, you will be able to determine the legal consequence of ambiguous 'aw' statements.

Guided Path
1
Define the particle 'aw' according to the Hanafi school
Read the definition: 'aw' is for referencing one of the mentioned things without specification. Understand that this concept is vague and not suitable for a personal ruling like freedom or divorce until clarified.
The definition applies to both akhbar and insha' but its effect differs.
2
Distinguish akhbar (declarative) from insha' (performative) usage
In akhbar, 'aw' may appear with doubt due to the context (unknown report); in insha', it gives choice or permission because insha' establishes speech anew and cannot admit doubt.
Example: 'Zayd is sitting or standing' (akhbar) vs. 'I appoint you to sell this or this' (insha').
3
Analyze the dispute with opposing scholars
The text mentions that a group of usulis and grammarians hold that 'aw' is placed for doubt. The Hanafi response: doubt is not a meaning intended by the speaker; context may create doubt in akhbar, but the particle itself indicates one of two without specification.
The chosen view (Shams al-A'imma, Fakhr al-Islam) aligns with the majority of language scholars.
4
Apply the definition to legal examples
Work through the examples: manumission ('this slave is free or this' → ambiguity requires specification), agency (choice for each agent), divorce (immediate effect on third wife), and oaths (Zufar's view vs. Hanafi view on breaking oath).
In oaths, the Hanafi rule differs for negative oaths: 'aw' may give generality.
5
Formulate the legal principle (qā‘ida) from the discussion
Summarize: 'Aw' in insha' is for choice/permission; in akhbar it is for one of two without specification, and if the report is unknown, clarification is needed. This principle drives the rulings.
This qā‘ida is a sub-maxim (ḍābiṭ) under the broader rule of dealing with ambiguous language in legal statements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أصول الشاشي مع أحسن الحواشي فصل أو لتناول أحد المذكورين من غير تعيين. قوله [لتناول... إلخ ] أي: لنسبة أمر إلى أحد الشيئين لا على التعين أو لنسبة أحد الأمرين إلى شيء، وبالجملة مفاده و محصول معناه اعتبار المفهوم المردود أخذه من الدوران بين الشيئين فيؤول المعنى إلى مفهوم أحدهما أو معنى أحدهما لا على التعيين، وهذا مفهوم مجمل مبهم غير صالح لنزول الحكم الشخصي عليه كالحرّية والطلاق، ولهذا يحول الأمر إلى بيان القائل وتعيينه ويكون له ولاية ويجيزه القاضي عليه ففي المفردين تفيد ثبوت الحكم لأحدهما، كقولك: «جاءني زيد أو بكر»، كما تقول: زيد قاعد أو قائم»، وفي الجملتين تفيد حصول مضمون أحدهما كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَنِ اقْتُلُواْ أَنفُسَكُمْ أَوِ اخْرُجُوا مِن دِيَارِكُم [النساء : ٦٦]﴾، هذا هو مذهب عامة أهل اللغة وأيمة الأصول وهو مختار شمس الأيمة وفخر الإسلام وذهبت طائفة من الأصوليين وجماعة من النحويين إلى أنها موضوعة للـــشكّ وهو ليس بسديد؛ لأنّ الشك ليس معنى يقصد بالكلام وضعاً، بل هي موضوعة لأحد المذكورين من غير تعيين، نعم في الأخبارات يجيء الشكّ باعتبار محلّ الكلام وهو الخبر المجهول، ولذا لزم منـــه التخيير في الإنشاء؛ لأنّ الإنشاء لإثبات الكلام ابتداءً فلا يحتمل الشك، فإنّ محلّه الخبر فـ«أو» في الإنشاء للتخيير أو الإباحة مثلا على حسب ما يناسب المقام ففي الخبر المجهول لزم البيان وفي الإنشاء لزم التخيير بين أحد الأمرين فافهم. ولهذا لو قال: «هذا حر أو هذا» كان في الإبهام والترديد. ولو قال: «وكلت ببيع هذا العبد هذا أو هذا» كان الوكيل أحدهما ويباح البيع لكل واحد منهما. ولو قال لثلاث نسوة له: «هذه طالق أو هذه وهذه» طلقت إحدى الأوليين وطلقت الثالثة في الحال. قال زفر: إذا قال «لا أكلم هذا أو هذا وهذا» كان بمنزلة قوله: «لا أكلم أحد هذين وهذا» فلا يحنث ما لم يكلم أحد الأولين والثالث. وعندنا لو كلم الأول وحده يحنث ولو كلم أحد الآخرين لا يحنث ما لم يكلّمهما.
Principles of al-Shashi with Ahsan al-Hawashi. Section: 'Or' for referring to one of the mentioned things without specification. His statement [for referring... etc.] means: attributing a matter to one of two things not specifically, or attributing one of two matters to a thing, and in summary its purport and the gist of its meaning is consideration of the rejected concept taken from alternation between two things, so the meaning resolves to the concept of one of them or the meaning of one of them without specification. This concept is a summary and vague concept not suitable for the descent of a personal ruling upon it like freedom and divorce; therefore the matter is transferred to the clarification of the speaker and his specification, and he has the authority and the judge permits him. So in the two singulars it indicates the establishment of a ruling for one of them, like your saying: 'Zayd or Bakr came to me', just as you say: 'Zayd is sitting or standing'. And in the two sentences it indicates the occurrence of the content of one of them, like His statement the Exalted: 'And that you kill yourselves or leave your homes' (Quran 4:66). This is the madhhab of the majority of language scholars and the imams of usul; it is the chosen view of Shams al-A'imma and Fakhr al-Islam. A group of usuli scholars and a group of grammarians held that it is placed for doubt, which is not sound because doubt is not a meaning intended by speech by way of placing. Rather, it is placed for one of the mentioned things without specification. Indeed, in reports (akhbar) doubt comes due to the context of speech, which is the unknown report. Hence, choice is necessitated in performatives (insha') because performatives establish speech initially and do not admit doubt. So 'or' in performatives is for choice or permission, for example, according to what suits the context. So in the unknown report specification is necessary, and in performatives choice between the two matters is necessary. Understand. And therefore if he says: 'This slave is free or this', it is in ambiguity and hesitation. And if he says: 'I appointed you to sell this slave: this or this', the agent is one of them and the sale is permissible for each one of them. And if he says to his three wives: 'This one is divorced or this one and this one', one of the first two is divorced and the third is divorced immediately. Zufar said: If he says 'I will not speak to this one or this one and this one', it is like his saying: 'I will not speak to either of these two and this one', so he does not break his oath until he speaks to one of the first two and the third. According to us, if he speaks to the first alone he breaks his oath; if he speaks to one of the other two he does not break his oath until he speaks to both.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage from Usool al-Shashi defines the particle 'aw' (or) and its legal implications. The author states that 'or' is placed for one of the mentioned things without specification. The commentary explains that this concept is vague and cannot directly bear a specific legal ruling like freedom or divorce; therefore, the speaker must clarify. In declarative sentences (akhbar), context may introduce doubt, but in performative sentences (insha'), 'or' indicates choice or permission. The main text provides examples: 1) In a manumission statement ('this slave is free or this'), the owner must specify which slave is free. 2) In an agency contract ('I appointed you to sell this slave or this'), each agent may sell, and the sale is valid for either. 3) In a conditional divorce ('You are divorced or you and this one'), one of the first two is divorced and the third is immediately divorced. Then a dispute with Zufar is mentioned regarding oaths: Zufar says that in a negative oath ('I will not speak to this one or this one and this one'), the oath is only broken by speaking to one of the first two and the third. The Hanafi position is that speaking to the first alone breaks the oath, but speaking to one of the others does not until both are spoken to. This is because in negative oaths, 'or' gives generality, while in positive statements like divorce, it gives alternation. The Hanafi position is based on the principle that 'or' in insha' gives choice or permission, and in akhbard (especially negative) it gives generality. This passage is a classic Hanafi usul discussion on the particle 'aw'.

Key Terms
أو (aw): A particle indicating one of the mentioned things without specification; in performatives (insha') it denotes choice or permission.
الإنشاء (al-inshā'): Performative speech: utterances that bring about a state of affairs (e.g., divorce, sale, oath) rather than reporting an existing fact.
الخبر (al-khabar): Declarative speech: utterances that report a fact and can be true or false.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the effect of 'aw' in a performative statement like 'I appointed you to sell this slave or this'?
A) The agency is invalid due to ambiguity.
B) Each of the two agents may sell, and the sale is permissible for either.
C) Only one agent may sell, and the other is excluded.
D) The agent must seek clarification from the principal.

Key Takeaway
The particle 'aw' in Hanafi usul is defined as indicating one of two without specification, and in performatives it gives choice/permission—a distinction critical for interpreting legal speech.

The Particle 'Or' (أو) in Hanafi Usul: Affirmative vs Negative Contexts
Explains legal effects of particle 'or' via examples of divorce, oath, agency, dower, and tashahhud.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule regarding the particle 'aw' to determine whether it implies choice or generality in affirmative and negative legal statements.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, 'aw' in affirmative gives choice; in negation, it generalizes over individuals.

The particle 'aw' (or) appears frequently in legal language, but its meaning changes dramatically depending on context. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi usul principle through five classical cases: divorce, oath, agency, dower, and the tashahhud in prayer. Understanding this principle is essential for accurate legal interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context: affirmative or negative
Determine whether the statement containing 'aw' is an affirmation (e.g., command, statement of fact) or a negation. This is the primary factor.
2
Apply the core Hanafi rule
If affirmative, 'aw' gives the subject a choice between the mentioned options. If negative, 'aw' generalizes over the individuals, making each independently negated.
3
Check for additional particles
Note if 'and' (waw) joins items, as this can combine them into a single unit for the purposes of negation or affirmation.
e.g., 'this or this and that' – the last two are conjoined.
4
Derive the ruling for the specific case
Apply the rule to each example: divorce, oath, agency, dower, prayer.
Ensure consistency with the Hanafi position.
5
Note intra-madhhab differences
Recognize where Zufar or the two disciples disagreed, and understand the thamarah al-khilaf.
The tarjih (preferred view) is stated in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل أو لتناول أحد المذكورين يبيعه، ولو قال لثلاث نسوة له: «هذه طالق أو هذه وهذه» طلقت إحدى الأوليين وطلقت الثالثة في الحال ويكون الخيار للزوج في بيان المطلقة منهما على هذا قال زفر: إذا قال «لا أكلم هذا أو هذا وهذا» كان بمنزلة قوله: «لا أكلم أحد هذين وهذا» فلا يحنث ما لم يكلم أحد الأولين والثالث، وعندنا لو كلم الأول وحده يحنث ولو كلم أحد الآخرين لا يحنث مالم يكلمهما قال: «بع هذا العبد أو هذا» كان له أن يبيع أحدهما أيهما شاء ولو دخل «أو» في المهر بأن تزوجها على هذا أو على هذا يحكم مهر المثل عند أبي حنيفة؛ وعندهما لا وعلى هذا قلنا : التشهد ليس بركن في الصلاة؛ لأن قوله عليه السلام: «إذا قلت هذا
