فيقع عليهما الطلاق) (قوله [وهذه] فإذا قال كذلك فالزوج بالخيار في بيان المطلقة، فكذلك في القول المذكور؛ لأنه بمنزلة هذا القول) (قوله [لا يحنث ما لم يكلّمهما] لأنّ الثابت بـ«أو» واحد غير معين، فيعمّ في موضع النفي عموم الأفراد، ويكون كلّ فرد منفياً عليحدة فيصير تقدير الكلام لا أكلم هذا ولا هذا»، فلما قال: «وهذا» بواو الجمع فقد جمعه إلى الثاني بنفي، فشاركه فصار كأنه قال: «لا أكلم هذا ولا هذين»، ولو قال هكذا يحنث لو كلّم الأوّل ولا يحنث لو كلّم أحد الآخرين ما لم يكلّمهما، والقياس على مسئلة الطلاق غير مستقيم؛ لأنّ الثابت بـ«أو» فيها إحداهما غير معين في موضع الإثبات فيختص وكانت المطلّقة :أي: إحدى الأوليين غير معيّن؛ لأنّ «أو» دخلت بينهما ، فلمّا قال: «وهذه» معطوفة على المطلقة منهما وهي غير معينة، فصار كأنه قال: «إحداكما طالق وهذه»، فلو قال هكذا تطلق الثالثة وتخيير الزوج بين الأوليين فكذا هاهنا) (قوله [أن يبيع أحدهما ... إلخ] لأنّ كلمة «أو» في موضع الإنشاء للتخيير؛ لأنّ قولك: «اضرب زيداً أو عمراً» لتناول أحدهما غير معيّن والأمر للإيتمار ولا يتصوّر الإيتمار بإيقاع الفعل في غير عين، فيثبت التخيير ضرورة التمكن من الايتمار) (قوله [ولو دخل... إلخ] الأصل فيه أنّ الأصل في المهر وهو مهر المثل وإنما يرجح المسمّى عليه بعارض التسمية، فإذا كان المسمّى غير مسمّى معين بل مبهماً صير إلى مهر المثل الذي هو الأصل عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله) (قوله [يحكم... إلخ] يعني: لو أدخل لفظ «أو» في المهر بأن قال: «تزوّجتك على هذا ألف درهم أو على هذا مئة دينار» مثلاً يحكم بمهر المثل عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله؛ لأنّ الموجب الأصلي في باب النكاح مهر المثل كالقيمة في باب البيع، وإنّما العدول عنه إذا كانت التسمية معلومة قطعا و لم توجد؛ لأنّ دخول كلمة «أو» يمنع كون المسمّى معلوماً قطعاً فوجب المصير إليه، وقالا إنها يوجب التخيير وللزوج أن يعطي أحد المهرين أيهما شاء، لكنّا نقول: إنّ كلمة «أو» وضع لتناول أحد الأمرين وهو مجهول غير معين، فإذا فسدت التسمية بجهالة يصار إلى موجبه الأصلي، وأمّا التخيير فإنّما يثبت ضرورة التمكن من الايتمار في الطلب كالأمر، وفي هذه المسئلة لم يوجد الأمر فلا يثبت التخيير) (قوله [في الصلاة] أي: في القعدة الأخيرة على طريق ذكر الكلّ وإرادة البعض، كما في قوله تعالى: يَجْعَلُونَ أَصابعَهُمْ في آذانهم الآية) (قوله [إذا قلت هذا] أي: قرأت التشهد و أنت قاعد؛ لأن قرأة التشهد لم تشرع إلا في حالة القعود) (قوله بأحدهما] أي علق الإتمام بأحدهما؛ لأنّ «أو» لتناول أحد المذكورين وهو القعدة أو قراءة التشهد فيكون أحدهما فرضاً)
Chapter on 'or' for indicating one of the mentioned things. He sells it, and if he says to three of his wives: 'This one is divorced or this one and this one,' then one of the first two is divorced and the third is divorced immediately, and the husband has the choice to specify which of the two is divorced. Based on this, Zufar said: If he says 'I will not speak to this one or this one and this one,' it is like saying 'I will not speak to either of these two and this one,' so he does not break his oath until he speaks to one of the first two and the third. In our view, if he speaks to the first alone, he breaks his oath; if he speaks to one of the others, he does not break his oath unless he speaks to both. He said: 'Sell this slave or this one,' so he may sell either one he wishes. If 'or' enters into the dower, such that he marries her on this or on that, Abu Hanifa rules that she gets the proper dower (mahr al-mithl); according to the two disciples, no. Based on this we said: The tashahhud is not a pillar of prayer, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'If you say this or do this, your prayer is complete.' He made completion conditional upon one of them, so it is not obligatory. (Commentary on the text: [And the third is divorced] meaning because the third is conjoined to the divorced one by 'waw', and conjunction with a particle of combining is like combining with a collective word, so it is as if he combined one of the first two and the third, so divorce falls on both. [And this] So if he says thus, the husband has the choice to specify the divorced one, so likewise in the mentioned statement. [He does not break his oath unless he speaks to both] because what is established by 'or' is one unspecified, so in the context of negation it generalizes over individuals, making each individual negated separately, so the implied wording is 'I will not speak to this one nor to this one.' When he said 'and this one' with the conjunctive waw, he joined it to the second in negation, so it becomes as if he said 'I will not speak to this one nor to these two.' If he says this, he breaks his oath if he speaks to the first, but not if he speaks to one of the others unless he speaks to both. The analogy to the divorce case is not sound, because what is established by 'or' there is one of them unspecified in an affirmative context, so it is specific. [That he may sell either one...] because the word 'or' in a performative context indicates choice; for your statement 'Strike Zayd or Amr' indicates one unspecified, and the command is to be obeyed, and obedience cannot be conceived with an unspecified act, so choice is established by necessity to enable obedience. [If 'or' enters...] The principle is that the original in dower is the proper dower, and the named dower is given preference only due to the occasion of naming. If the named dower is unspecified and ambiguous, recourse is to the proper dower, which is the original according to Abu Hanifa. [He rules...] means: If he uses 'or' in the dower, such as saying 'I marry you on this thousand dirhams or on this hundred dinars,' Abu Hanifa rules proper dower; according to them it gives choice and the husband may give whichever of the two he wishes. We say: The word 'or' is placed to indicate one of two things, which is unknown and unspecified. When the naming is invalid due to ambiguity, recourse is to the original. As for choice, it is established only by necessity for obedience in commands, and in this case there is no command, so choice is not established. [In the prayer] meaning in the final sitting, in the way of mentioning the whole and intending part, as in the verse 'They put their fingers in their ears.' [If you say this] means you recite the tashahhud while sitting, because recitation of tashahhud is only prescribed in the sitting position. [By one of them] means he made completion conditional upon one of them; because 'or' indicates one of the mentioned things, i.e., the sitting or recitation of tashahhud, so one of them is obligatory.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage is a chapter on the usul rule regarding the particle 'أو' (or) in legal language. It presents several case studies from different areas of fiqh. The rule is that 'أو' indicates one of two or more things without specifying which, but its application varies by context. In the divorce case, when a husband says 'this one is divorced or this one and this one,' the third wife is divorced immediately because she is conjoined with 'and' (واو) to the intended one, creating a collective effect. The husband retains the choice to specify which of the first two is divorced. In the oath case, Zufar's position is critiqued. The Hanafi view (our scholars) holds that in negations, 'or' actually generalizes over individuals, so specifying each individually. Thus, if someone says 'I will not speak to this one or this one and this one,' it means he will not speak to any of them; speaking to the first alone breaks the oath, but speaking to one of the other two does not break it unless both are spoken to. In agency, 'or' gives the agent the choice to sell either slave. In dower, Abu Hanifa rules that if the dower is specified with 'or' (e.g., either 1000 dirhams or 100 dinars), the marriage contract is valid but the dower becomes ambiguous, so recourse is to the proper dower (mahr al-mithl). The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that it gives the husband the choice to pay either, but the text rejects this because 'or' does not create a command here. Finally, in prayer, the hadith 'If you say this or do this, your prayer is complete' uses 'or' to indicate that either the tashahhud recitation or the sitting (at its duration) is sufficient, meaning neither is obligatory individually; thus tashahhud is not a pillar (rukn) but a wajib. The passage uses analogy and textual analysis to demonstrate these principles.

Key Terms
أو (aw): A particle indicating disjunction (تخيير) or generality depending on context (affirmative vs. negative).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a man marries a woman on the dower of 'either 1000 dirhams or 100 dinars,' what is the ruling?
A) The marriage is invalid due to ambiguity.
B) The wife receives the proper dower (mahr al-mithl).
C) The husband may choose which amount to give.
D) The wife may choose which amount to receive.

Key Takeaway
The particle 'aw' in Hanafi usul is context-sensitive: in affirmative contexts it gives choice, in negative contexts it generalizes over individuals.

The Usul Rule of 'Aw' (Or) in Hanafi Fiqh
Analyzing the word 'aw' in positive and negative contexts with examples from sale, marriage, and prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule of 'aw' to identify its legal effect in commands, negation, and contracts, and evaluate its role in the tashahhud dispute.

Core Idea
'Aw' in commands means choice AND permissibility of both; in negation, it negates each individually.

The Arabic particle 'aw' (أو) appears frequently in legal texts – from sales contracts to prophetic hadith. Its legal meaning, however, shifts dramatically depending on context. In this lesson, we dissect the Hanafi usul rule for 'aw', tracing its application through three distinct cases: a sale agency, a marriage dower, and the prayer tashahhud. You will learn why Imam Abu Hanifa ruled that an uncertain dower defaults to mahr al-mithl, and how the same particle in the hadith 'When you say this or do this, your prayer is complete' proves that tashahhud is wajib, not fard.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal contexts of 'aw'
Locate the three contexts in the source text where 'aw' is used: (1) in a positive command (agency sale), (2) in a negative oath, and (3) in a marriage dower contract. Note how each context changes the legal effect.
2
Analyze 'aw' in commands: the agency example
When the agent is told 'Sell this slave or this slave', he may choose either. Why? Because 'aw' in imperative contexts implies takhyir (choice) and also ibaha (permissibility of both) – the agent could even sell both if he wishes.
Hanafi: choice is a necessity for compliance, and from that necessity flows general permissibility.
3
Analyze 'aw' in negation: the oath example
If someone says 'I will not speak to Zayd or Amr', he breaks his oath by speaking to just one. In negation, 'aw' treats each item individually (istighraq) – the prohibition applies to each separately.
The word 'aw' here is a nakira in siyaq al-nafi, which generalizes each individually.
4
Analyze 'aw' in contracts without command: the dower dispute
When a man marries on 'a thousand dirhams or a hundred dinars', Abu Hanifa rules that the dower is mahr al-mithl because 'aw' makes the specification uncertain. His students (Sahibayn) disagree, arguing that the husband can choose. The commentator defends Abu Hanifa: 'aw' in contracts (no command) does not create choice but uncertainty, so we revert to the default.
The key distinction: choice is only established when there is a command to obey (amr). In a contract, there is no command, only a declaration.
5
Apply the rule to the tashahhud hadith
The Prophet said: 'When you say this (tashahhud) or do this (sit for its duration), your prayer is complete.' Since 'aw' in positive commands gives a choice, and sitting is fard by consensus, tashahhud cannot be fard – it is wajib, and its omission requires sajda sahw. The Hanafis adhere to the literal meaning of 'aw' (reality of completion), rejecting the Shafi'i metaphorical interpretation ('nearness to completion').
The Hadith of 'Arafat ('When he stands at Arafat, his Hajj is complete') is cited as a counterargument, but the Hanafis distinguish that case as a metaphor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل أو لتناول أحد المذكورين

قال: «بع هذا العبد أو هذا» كان له أن يبيع أحدهما أيهما شاء. ولو دخل «أو» في المهر بأن تزوجها على هذا أو على هذا يحكم بمهر المثل عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأنّ اللفظ يتناول أحدهما والموجب الأصلي مهر المثل فيترجح ما يشابهه، وعندهما لا. وعلى هذا قلنا: التشهد ليس بركن في الصلاة؛ لأن قوله عليه السلام: «إذا قلت هذا أو فعلت هذا فقد تمت صلوتك» علق الإتمام بأحدهما فلا يشترط كلّ واحد منهما وقد شرطت القعدة بالاتفاق فلا يشترط قراءة التشهد. ثم هذه الكلمة في مقام النفي يوجب نفي كلّ واحد من المذكورين حتى لو قال: «لا أكلّم هذا أو هذا» يحنث إذا كلّم أحدهما. وفي الإثبات يتناول أحدهما مع صفة التخيير، كقولهم: «خذ هذا أو ذلك» ومن ضرورة التخيير عموم الإباحة.

قال الشارح: لأنّ كلمة «أو» في موضع الإنشاء للتخيير؛ لأنّ قولك: «اضرب زيداً أو عمراً» لتناول أحدهما غير معيّن والأمر للإيتمار ولا يتصوّر الإيتمار بإيقاع الفعل في غير عين، فيثبت التخيير ضرورة التمكن من الايتمار. ولو دخل «أو» في المهر بأن قال: «تزوّجتك على هذا ألف درهم أو على هذا مئة دينار» يحكم بمهر المثل عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأنّ الموجب الأصلي في باب النكاح مهر المثل كالقيمة في باب البيع، وإنّما العدول عنه إذا كانت التسمية معلومة قطعا و لم توجد؛ لأنّ دخول كلمة «أو» يمنع كون المسمّى معلوماً قطعاً فوجب المصير إليه، وقالا إنها يوجب التخيير وللزوج أن يعطي أحد المهرين أيهما شاء، لكنّا نقول: إنّ كلمة «أو» وضع لتناول أحد الأمرين وهو مجهول غير معين، فإذا فسدت التسمية بجهالة يصار إلى موجبه الأصلي، وأمّا التخيير فإنّما يثبت ضرورة التمكن من الايتمار في الطلب كالأمر، وفي هذه المسئلة لم يوجد الأمر فلا يثبت التخيير فتدبّر. وعند الشافعي رحمه الله التشهد فرض وعند أصحابنا واجب حتى تجب سجدة السهو إذا سهى عنه، لكنّ الصلاة تتم بدونه لوجود أركانها لما ذكرنا من التمسك بكلمة «أو» في الحديث، فإن قيل: لفظ الإتمام لا يدلّ على أنه لم يبق فرضاً بعده كما في قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «إذا وقف بعرفات فقد تم حجه»، فإنّه بقي عليه طواف الزيارة بالإجماع، قلنا: حقيقة الإتمام في شيء أنه لم يبق بعده جزء من أجزائه، فلم يبق التشهد فرضاً لفرضية القعدة بالاتفاق فأمّا أن يراد به الأشراف وهي القرب فهو مجاز، كما روي عن عبد الله بن عباس رضي الله عنهما قال عليه السلام: «إذا رفعت رأسك من آخر السجدة فقد تمت صلاتك»، وإرادة المجاز وهو القرب منها في بعض الصور لا يدلّ على ترك الحقيقة في اللفظ ولا يصار إلى المجاز إلا عند تعذر العمل بالحقيقة، وحديث التشهد غير متعذر عملاً. وقوله: يحنث إذا كلّم أحدهما لما سبق أنها يتناول أحد المذكورين وهو نكرة في سياق النفي فيعم على وجه الانفراد. ولا يثبت الخيار في تعيين أحدهما؛ لأنّ الكلّ صار منفياً ولو بقي «أو» على حقيقته لوجب التخيير؛ لأنه يكون أحدهما منفياً فيكون له ولاية التعيين في أحدهما كما لو كان في الإثبات. وفي الإثبات يتناول أحدهما مع صفة التخيير، هذا في مقام الإنشاء والطلب، كقولهم: «خذ هذا أو ذلك» ومن ضرورة التخيير عموم الإباحة أي إباحة كلّ واحد من المذكورين ألا ترى أنه إذا يقال: «جالس الفقهاء أو المحدثين» كان معناه عندهم جالس أحدهما أو كليهما إن شئت.
Section: 'Aw' (or) for taking one of the two mentioned things. He said: 'Sell this slave or this slave' – he may sell whichever he wishes. If 'aw' enters into the dower such that he marries her on this or on this, it is ruled by the dower of the like according to Abu Hanifa, because the word takes one of them and the original obligatory is the dower of the like so what resembles it is preferred; according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) no. And on this we said: the tashahhud is not a pillar in prayer, because his saying (peace be upon him): 'When you say this or do this, your prayer is complete' attached completion to one of them, so each one is not required; while the sitting is required by consensus, so reciting tashahhud is not required. Then this word in the context of negation necessitates negation of each one of the mentioned things, so if he says: 'I will not speak to this one or this one', he breaks his oath if he speaks to one of them. And in affirmation it takes one of them with the attribute of choice, like their saying: 'Take this or that'; and from the necessity of choice is permissibility of both.

The commentator said: Because the word 'aw' in the position of command is for choice; because your saying 'Strike Zayd or Amr' is for taking one of them unspecified, and the command is for compliance, and compliance with performing the act without specification is inconceivable, so choice is established by necessity to enable compliance. If 'aw' enters into the dower such that he says: 'I marry you on this thousand dirhams or on this one hundred dinars', it is ruled by the dower of the like according to Abu Hanifa, because the original obligator in marriage is the dower of the like like the price in sale; deviation from it only occurs if the specification is known definitively and it is not present; because the entry of 'aw' prevents the specified from being known definitively, so recourse to the original is obligatory. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it obligates choice and the husband may give whichever of the two dowers he wishes, but we say: the word 'aw' is placed for taking one of two matters and it is unknown unspecified; when the specification is invalidated by ignorance, recourse to its original obligator is taken. As for choice, it is established by necessity to enable compliance in request like command, but in this issue there is no command, so choice is not established, so reflect. According to al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him), tashahhud is obligatory (fard), and according to our companions it is wajib such that the prostration of forgetfulness becomes obligatory if he forgets it, but the prayer is complete without it due to the existence of its pillars because of what we mentioned of clinging to the word 'aw' in the hadith. If it is said: the word 'completion' does not indicate that nothing remains obligatory after it, as in his saying: 'When he stands at Arafat, his Hajj is complete', yet tawaf al-ziyara remains upon him by consensus, we say: the reality of completion in something is that no part of its parts remains after it; thus tashahhud does not remain obligatory due to the obligation of the sitting by consensus; so if what is meant is the nearness, it is a metaphor, as narrated from Ibn Abbas: 'When you raise your head from the last prostration, your prayer is complete'; and intending the metaphor (nearness) in some cases does not indicate abandoning the literal meaning, and one does not resort to metaphor except when literal application is impossible, and the hadith of tashahhud is not impossible to apply literally. As for his statement: 'he breaks his oath if he speaks to one of them' because as previously, it takes one of the mentioned things and it is an indefinite in the context of negation so it generalizes individually. And choice in specifying one of them is not established because the whole becomes negated; if 'aw' remained on its literal meaning, choice would be obligatory because one of them is negated so he would have the authority to specify one of them as in affirmation. And in affirmation it takes one of them with the attribute of choice; this is in the context of command and request, like their saying: 'Take this or that'; and from the necessity of choice is general permissibility of each of the mentioned things; do you not see that when it is said: 'Sit with the jurists or the hadith scholars', its meaning according to them is sit with one of them or both if you wish.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is an usul rule extraction from the matn of al-Shashi, expanded by the commentator (Ahsan al-Hawashi). The central topic is the linguistic-legal particle 'aw' (or) and how its meaning shifts depending on context: positive command, negative statement, and marital dower. The passage begins with a clear example from agency: if a principal tells his agent 'Sell this slave or this slave', the agent may choose which to sell. This is because 'aw' in commands (insha) indicates choice (takhyir) out of necessity for compliance. The second example concerns marriage dower: if a man marries a woman specifying two different dowers with 'or', Imam Abu Hanifa rules that the dower of the like (mahr al-mithl) applies because the 'aw' makes the specification uncertain, and the default in marriage is the dower of the like. His two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, holding that the husband may choose any dower. The commentator defends Abu Hanifa's view: 'aw' denotes one of two unspecified things, and such ignorance invalidates the specification—choice is only applicable in commands, not in contracts where no command to obey exists. The third example derives from a hadith about prayer completion: the Prophet said, 'When you say this (i.e., tashahhud) or do this (i.e., sit for its duration), your prayer is complete.' The Hanafis use this to argue that tashahhud is not a fard pillar but only wajib, because the prayer's completion is tied to one of two alternatives (sitting or recitation). Since sitting is agreed to be fard, recitation cannot be fard as well—it is merely wajib, requiring sajda sahw if omitted. The commentary then defends this against the Shafi'i position. Finally, the passage examines 'aw' in negation: when someone says 'I will not speak to Zayd or Amr', they violate their oath by speaking to just one, because 'aw' in negation negates each individually (nakira in siyaq al-nafi). In contrast, in positive affirmation, 'aw' implies choice and also general permissibility of both options (e.g., 'Sit with the jurists or the traditionists' allows either or both). Thus the commentator establishes a nuanced usul rule: the function of 'aw' depends on whether it occurs in an imperative, a declarative contract, or a negative oath, with specific Hanafi positions in each case.

Key Terms
أو (aw): A particle indicating one of two mentioned things, with different implications in commands (choice) vs. negation (each individually) and in contracts (uncertainty).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling when a man marries a woman on 'a thousand dirhams or a hundred dinars'?
A) The husband must pay both amounts.
B) The husband may choose which to pay.
C) The wife gets the dower of the like (mahr al-mithl).
D) The marriage is invalid due to uncertainty.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, 'aw' in positive commands indicates choice and general permissibility, in negation it negates each individually, and in contracts without a command it creates uncertainty leading to default values.

The Particle 'Aw' in Negation: Oath Implications
Analyzing the legal effect of the particle ‘aw’ in oath contexts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for the particle ‘aw’ in negative contexts to determine whether an oath is broken.

Core Idea
In negation, ‘aw’ negates each item individually—speaking to one breaks the oath.

In this lesson, we examine how the particle ‘aw’ functions differently in negative versus affirmative contexts. This distinction is crucial for correctly ruling on oaths and other legal statements. The Hanafi school holds that in negation, ‘aw’ operates like ‘waw’ to negate each conjunct separately, a view supported by linguistic principles and Quranic usage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context: negation or affirmation
Read the phrase carefully to determine whether it is negative (e.g., ‘la aful...’) or affirmative. The rule differs fundamentally.
Look for particles like ‘la’, ‘ma’, ‘lam’, etc.
2
Apply the Hanafi rule for ‘aw’ in negation
If the context is negative, ‘aw’ negates each of the mentioned items individually. For example, ‘la uqallimu Zaydan aw ‘Amran’ means ‘I will not speak to Zayd and I will not speak to ‘Amr’.
Contrast with affirmative where ‘aw’ gives choice (takhyeer).
3
Derive the ruling for the oath
Since each item is separately negated, speaking to any one of them violates the oath. The oath-taker consequently breaks his oath.
No need to speak to all; one is sufficient.
4
Verify with Quranic evidence
The Quran uses ‘aw’ in affirmative contexts (e.g., 5:89) to indicate choice, supporting the pattern that in negation the opposite holds. Also note the usage of ‘aw’ to mean ‘hatta’ (until) in 3:128, showing contextual flexibility.
The Hanafi method respects the context over a fixed meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل: أو لتناول أحد المذكورين. بيننا وبين الشافعي رحمه الله. يشترط كل واحد منهما وقد شرطت القعدة بالاتفاق فلا يشترط قراءة التشهد، ثم هذه الكلمة في مقام النفي يوجب نفي كل واحد من المذكورين. حتى لو قال: «لا أكلّم هذا أو هذا» يحنث إذا كلّم أحدهما. وفي الإثبات يتناول أحدهما مع صفة التخيير، كقولهم: «خذ هذا أو ذلك» ومن ضرورة التخيير عموم الإباحة. قال الله تعالى: فَكَفَّارَتُهُ إِطْعَامُ عَشَرَةِ مَسَاكِينَ مِنْ أَوْسَطِ مَا تُطْعِمُونَ أَهْلِيكُمْ أَوْ كسوتُهُمْ أَوْ تَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَة [المائدة: ٨٩]، وقد يكون «أو» بمعنى حتى. قال الله تعالى: لَيْسَ لَكَ مِنَ الْأَمْرِ شَيْءٌ أَوْ يَتُوبَ عَلَيْهِمْ ﴾ [آل عمران: ۱۲۸]، أي حتى يتوب عليهم.
Chapter: 'Or' for addressing one of the mentioned. Between us and al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him. Each one of them is required, and the sitting has been required by consensus, so the recitation of the tashahhud is not required. Then this word in the context of negation necessitates the negation of every single one of the mentioned. So if he says, 'I will not speak to this one or this one,' he breaks his oath if he speaks to either of them. And in the affirmative, it addresses one of them with the attribute of choice, as they say, 'Take this or that.' And from the necessity of choice is the generality of permissibility. Allah Almighty said: 'Then its expiation is feeding ten needy people from the average of what you feed your families or clothing them or freeing a slave' [Al-Ma'idah 5:89]. And 'or' can be used in the sense of 'until.' Allah Almighty said: 'You have nothing of the matter, or He turns to them in mercy' [Aal-E-Imran 3:128], meaning until He turns to them in mercy.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage analyzes the particle 'aw' (or) in legal and oath contexts. The author first explains that in negation (nafi), 'aw' negates each of the mentioned items individually. For example, if a person swears 'I will not speak to Zaid or Amr,' he breaks his oath by speaking to either one, because each is separately negated. This contrasts with affirmative contexts where 'aw' gives choice, as in 'Take this or that.' The author then cites the Quranic verse on expiation for an oath (5:89) to illustrate 'aw' in a context of choice among three options (feeding, clothing, freeing a slave), implying permissibility of any one. Finally, the note states that 'aw' can also mean 'until' (hatta), citing 3:128. This shows the Hanafi method of giving each usage its appropriate legal effect based on context.

Key Terms
أو ('aw): A particle that can indicate choice (takhyeer) in affirmative contexts, negation of each individual in negative contexts, or meaning 'until' (hatta) when the conjuncts are incompatible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone swears 'لا أكلّم زيدا أو عمرا' (I will not speak to Zaid or Amr) and then speaks to Amr only, what is the ruling?
A) He does not break his oath because he only spoke to one.
B) He breaks his oath because each is negated individually.
C) He breaks his oath only if he speaks to both.
D) It depends on his intention at the time of the oath.

Key Takeaway
The particle 'aw' in negation negates each of the mentioned items individually, so speaking to any one breaks the oath.

The Hanafi Rule for 'Hatta' in Conditional Oaths
Defines the rule for 'hatta' when it cannot be a true ghaya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that 'hatta' in a conditional oath with a single doer is interpreted as pure conjunction, and derive the ruling for a given scenario.

Core Idea
When the condition and result share the same agent, 'hatta' becomes 'and'—pure conjunction, not a temporal end.

This lesson explores a subtle Hanafi usul principle: the particle 'hatta' (until) does not always indicate a temporal limit. In conditional oaths where the same person performs both the condition and the result, 'hatta' must be reinterpreted as pure conjunction to avoid the logical impossibility of one penalizing oneself. Understanding this rule is crucial for correctly evaluating oaths and conditional statements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the particle and its default meaning
Recognize that 'hatta' normally indicates the end-point (ghaya) of an action, as in 'I will wait until you come'.
2
Recognize the logical problem
Notice that when both the condition and the result actions are attributed to the same person (e.g., 'If I do not come until I eat'), it is impossible for one's own action to be a penalty for another of one's own actions.
The one who imposes the penalty must be different from the one on whom the penalty is imposed.
3
Apply the Hanafi rule
Because of this impossibility, 'hatta' is divested of its ghaya meaning and carried as pure conjunction (عطف محض), meaning 'and'.
The two actions are combined into a single condition.
4
Work through the example from Imam Muhammad
A man says: 'My slave is free if I do not come to you until I eat lunch at your house today.' He comes but does not eat. Under the rule, the condition is both coming and eating; missing either triggers the penalty. Hence he is sinful (breaks his oath) and his slave is freed.
5
Generalize the rule's application
This rule applies only in conditional sentences (e.g., with 'in' or 'in lam') where the same individual is the subject of both the condition and the result.
It does not apply when different persons are involved.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل حتى للغاية. من غير دلالة على غاية أو مجازاة يصلح الآخر جزاء للأوّل حمل على العطف المحض. مثاله ما قال محمد رحمه الله: إذا قال: «عبدي حرّ إن لم آتك حتى أتغدّي عندك اليوم» أو «إن لم تأتني فعبدي حرّ» فأتاه فلم يتغد عنده في ذلك اليوم حنث. وذلك لأنه لَمّا أضيف كلّ واحد من الفعلين إلى ذات واحد لا يصلح أن يكون فعله جزاء لفعله فيحمل على العطف المحض فيكون المجموع شرطا للبر، لأن المجازي بالكسر يجب أن يكون غير المجازي بالفتح.
Section on 'hatta' for the end-point. If it indicates neither an end-point nor a penalty, and the second [action] is suitable as a penalty for the first, it is carried as pure conjunction. Example of what Muhammad [al-Shaybani] said: If he says: 'My slave is free if I do not come to you until I eat lunch at your house today,' or 'If you do not come to me, my slave is free,' then he came but did not eat lunch at his place that day, he is sinful. That is because when each of the two actions is attributed to one entity, it is not valid for his action to be a penalty for his action, so it is carried as pure conjunction, making the total the condition for fulfillment, because the one who imposes the penalty must be other than the one on whom the penalty is imposed.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage explains a Hanafi usul rule about the particle 'hatta' (until). When 'hatta' appears in a conditional sentence and both the condition and the result are actions of the same person (the speaker), it cannot indicate a true end-point because one cannot punish or reward oneself. Therefore, 'hatta' is interpreted as pure conjunction (عطف محض), meaning the two actions are combined as a single condition. The example from Imam Muhammad: a man says 'My slave is free if I do not come to you until I eat lunch at your house today.' If the man comes but does not eat, he breaks his oath and his slave is freed. The reasoning is that since the speaker is both the subject of the condition and the one bound by the result, 'hatta' must be read as 'and' rather than 'until', making the condition the occurrence of both actions (coming and eating) together. If either is missing, the condition is not met.

Key Terms
حتى (hatta): A particle indicating the end-point (ghaya) of an action; in this context, it is reinterpreted as conjuction due to the impossibility of one person penalizing oneself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example from Imam Muhammad, if the man says 'My slave is free if I do not come to you until I eat lunch at your house today,' then he comes but does not eat, what happens?
A) He is not sinful because he came.
B) He is sinful and his slave is freed.
C) He is sinful but his slave is not freed.
D) The condition is considered invalid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, when 'hatta' links two actions by the same person in a conditional oath, it is read as pure conjunction, making both actions necessary for the condition to be met.
